  /** Converts a <button> to look like an <a> tag. */
  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;
    border: 0;

    cursor: pointer;

    color: var(--chops-link-color);
    text-decoration: none;
    font-weight: var(--chops-link-font-weight);
    font-family: var(--chops-font-family);
  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */
    display: inline-flex;
    align-items: center;
    justify-content: center;
    text-decoration: none;
    transition: filter 0.3s ease-in-out, box-shadow 0.3s ease-in-out;
  }
  a.button:hover, .button:hover {

  }
  textarea, select, input {
    box-sizing: border-box;
    font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for
  * accessibility because styles will not always line up with semantically
  * appropriate heading levels.

  .medium-heading {

          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;

          width: 100%;

          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

          flex-grow: 0;

        }

          width: 100%;

          min-width: 50%;

          position: sticky;

          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {

          }

            width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

I don't think this is a security bug -- the preview page is showing the correct URL and nothing is being spoofed.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think this is a security bug -- the preview page is showing the correct URL and nothing is being spoofed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The HTML is:



<span class="line"><!---->The HTML is:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  <a href="



<span class="line"><!---->  &lt;a href="<!----></span>





http://www.google.com/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://www.google.com/"><!---->http://www.google.com/<!----></a>





"



<span class="line"><!---->"<!----></span>





 onclick="this.href='



<span class="line"><!----> onclick="this.href='<!----></span>





https://Websecgeeks.com/'">Priview



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://Websecgeeks.com/'&quot;>Priview"><!---->https://Websecgeeks.com/'"&gt;Priview<!----></a>





 This</a>



<span class="line"><!----> This&lt;/a&gt;<!----></span>



<br>

So the actual link is to



<span class="line"><!---->So the actual link is to<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://google.com"><!---->google.com<!----></a>





, and that's what the Preview uses. When you click instead, the click handler replaces the current window's location. There are a lot of ways that a site could intentionally trigger slightly different behavior for different ways a user interacts with a link (e.g., you could construct some HTML/JS that loads siteA.example if you click it but loads siteB.example if you Control+Click it, etc.).



<span class="line"><!---->, and that's what the Preview uses. When you click instead, the click handler replaces the current window's location. There are a lot of ways that a site could intentionally trigger slightly different behavior for different ways a user interacts with a link (e.g., you could construct some HTML/JS that loads siteA.example if you click it but loads siteB.example if you Control+Click it, etc.).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'll defer to the feature team on whether there is a reasonable way to catch some of the common cases of click handlers and stuff like that.



<span class="line"><!---->I'll defer to the feature team on whether there is a reasonable way to catch some of the common cases of click handlers and stuff like that.<!----></span>

It's going to be tough in general. Knowing if there is a click handler on the element itself won't help much against truly malicious actors because they can instead register on any ancestor node, or register for a different event in the click series (say, mouseup), or use any of a variety of other tricks.



<span class="line"><!---->It's going to be tough in general. Knowing if there is a click handler on the element itself won't help much against truly malicious actors because they can instead register on any ancestor node, or register for a different event in the click series (say, mouseup), or use any of a variety of other tricks.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Ultimately what appears in the omnibox *after* click is going to be much more reliable.



<span class="line"><!---->Ultimately what appears in the omnibox *after* click is going to be much more reliable.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





cc dcheng@ who's a general subject matter expert on such things; if you really want to tackle this you might also want to loop in estark@ for security UX



<span class="line"><!---->cc dcheng@ who's a general subject matter expert on such things; if you really want to tackle this you might also want to loop in estark@ for security UX<!----></span>

Comment #4



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c4"><!---->Comment #4<!----></a>





, I think this is at most Severity-Low, so the labels should be okay (and imply that it isn't urgent to fix, if we do decide it is worth fixing).



<span class="line"><!---->, I think this is at most Severity-Low, so the labels should be okay (and imply that it isn't urgent to fix, if we do decide it is worth fixing).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Do we have usage numbers for OnClick handlers? Do we know how disruptive suppressing UI features (like Preview Tab, but potentially others) would be? Note that I still don't think there is any actual spoofing going on here -- all of the Security UX shows the correct site identity. I consider this roughly in the same camp as a site using an open redirect to hide a link navigation.

> Does anyone know what the other context menu options do with this case? It would be useful to understand what "Open in new Tab" does. Also there may be new UI treatment in the context menu that previews the URL, so that might be helpful (though most users won't notice this). +Sinan in case he knows about these Context Menu questions.



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; Does anyone know what the other context menu options do with this case? It would be useful to understand what "Open in new Tab" does. Also there may be new UI treatment in the context menu that previews the URL, so that might be helpful (though most users won't notice this). +Sinan in case he knows about these Context Menu questions.<!----></span>

When we display the context menu, we hit test and capture any interesting attributes such as any link associated with the element under the cursor. This behavior might also differ if the context menu is invoked via a keyboard shortcut instead of with a right-click.



<span class="line"><!---->When we display the context menu, we hit test and capture any interesting attributes such as any link associated with the element under the cursor. <br>





In this case, what would happen is we would run the JS event handlers before we hit test for the context menu, so the link will already be changed by then.



<span class="line"><!---->In this case, what would happen is we would run the JS event handlers before we hit test for the context menu, so the link will already be changed by then.<!----></span>

Based on the video and my understanding, I don't think we consider this a security bug. The interaction isn't one atomic interaction where we display a misleading preview, and then clicking on the preview UX opens the wrong URL. Instead, the PoC requires dismissing the preview, and then clicking the link to navigate.



<span class="line"><!---->Based on the video and my understanding, I don't think we consider this a security bug. The interaction isn't one atomic interaction where we display a misleading preview, and then clicking on the preview UX opens the wrong URL. Instead, the PoC requires dismissing the preview, and then clicking the link to navigate.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I tested that clicking the [↗] in the preview pane opens a URL that matches the preview. If that were misleading, I think we would definitely consider this a security bug, but that's not the case here.



<span class="line"><!---->I tested that clicking the [↗] in the preview pane opens a URL that matches the preview. If that were misleading, I think we would definitely consider this a security bug, but that's not the case here.<!----></span>

          z-index: 999;

          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;

        .chops-autocomplete-container td {

          white-space: nowrap;

        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;

      </style>

          display: none;
